And how might some people in general use their bad characteristics in a way that helps them? Okay, so I believe there's no such thing as a bad characteristic or good characteristic. At least, no matter how bad a characteristic is in a certain context, when used appropriately, in a different context, can be an asset. So for example, again, one of my bad traits is I'm really stubborn. I'm a nonconformist, when everyone says this, I'll say, why can't we do something else? And it irritates the heck out of my teachers and my parents in the past. But I've learned to use that to my advantage. So again, when people told me in secondary school that you can't make it to junior college. You can't make it to university. That really motivates me to prove them wrong. And so that's how I've used it to my advantage. Another bad trait I would say, bad trait is that I'm slow learner. When I was young my friends could read a chapter of additional mathematics, calculus, and understand it the first time. Teacher could explain it the first time, they got it. I didn't get it. I had to read that same page three or four times before I got it. Teacher had to explain it a few times before I got it.
所以，正如你提到的，有时你并没有动力，事实上，有时你有一些不好的特质，而你在生活中也经历过这些不好的特质。那么你能告诉我一下，如何将不好的特质有时转变为好的特质？一般来说，人们如何利用他们的不良特质来帮助自己？

好的，我认为没有所谓的坏特质或好特质。至少，无论某种特质在特定的情况下有多么糟糕，如果在不同的背景下适当地使用，它都可以成为一种资产。例如，我的一个坏习惯就是我非常固执。当每个人都说“这样做不行”的时候，我会问，“为什么我们不能尝试其他方式？”这常常让我的老师和父母感到非常恼火。但我学会了将这一点转化为自己的优势。因此，当人们在中学时告诉我，你无法进入初级学院，无法上大学时，这真的激励我去证明他们是错的。这就是我如何利用我的固执。

另一个我认为是坏习惯的特质是我学习得很慢。当我年轻的时候，我的朋友可以在第一次阅读附加数学、微积分的章节时就理解它。老师第一次讲解时，他们就懂了。而我没有。我必须阅读同一页三到四次，才能理解。老师必须多解释几次，我才能明白。

And now I look back, that's a great asset, because now as a teacher myself, I'm now able to understand how slow learners like me process. And I'm able to take something which is complicated and make it really simple, so that anyone can learn. So again that has, I've used that to my advantage as well. So everything which is a liability can be looked at as an asset.
而现在回头看，这其实是一个很好的资产，因为现在作为一名老师，我能够理解像我这样的慢学习者是如何处理信息的。我能够将复杂的知识变得简单，让任何人都能学习。因此，我也将这一点转化为我的优势。所以，任何被视为负担的特质都可以被看作是资产。

We share so much in common, because sometimes I think my best trait as a teacher is that it's hard for me to understand things, and so I do find that once I understand them, I can only understand it if it's made simple. But once I do make it simple, it's much easier to explain to other people. If I was smarter, in some sense, I couldn't be as effective a teacher. Absolutely. So, what advice do you have for someone who feels that their job skills are becoming obsolete? Which is a very common thing- Sure. To happen today. What can people do to be more resilient in their careers? So the only way to create resilience to protect your career, is to ensure that you make yourself obsolete before someone makes you obsolete, all right. And the only way to do that, again, is through constant and never-ending improvement. And the first thing is an attitude, to ask yourself if what I'm doing now is the same thing I'm doing a year ago, something's wrong. It's gotta be better, it's gotta change.
所以，唯一创造韧性以保护你的职业的方法，就是在别人让你过时之前，先让自己变得过时。只有通过不断地、永不停息地改进，你才能做到这一点。首先，你需要有一个正确的心态，问自己：我现在所做的事情是否和一年前做的一样？如果是，那就有问题了。你必须在某些方面变得更好，必须有所改变。

And always ask yourself, how can I do something better than I did in the past. And I've always done that my life. So I love learning, and I've always been a lifelong learner. So I go online and I take courses all the time relating to my field or even outside of my field. And that allows me to have the breadth of knowledge and expertise to be able to do anything. So, if my business, if I knock on wood, were to be obsolete tomorrow, I can start a new business doing something else, adding value to the world with the portable skills I've created.
总是问问自己，如何能比过去做得更好。我一生中一直都是这样做的。我热爱学习，并且一直是一个终身学习者。因此，我会在线上不断参加与我所在领域相关或甚至是与我领域无关的课程。这让我拥有广泛的知识和专业技能，能够做任何事情。所以，如果我的生意，敲敲木头，明天变得过时，我可以开始一项新的业务，做其他事情，利用我所掌握的可转移技能为世界创造价值。

So, I know that luck plays a role in success in life. How can someone encourage luck? Okay. If you hear a lot of people speak, they say I got lucky, and I got lucky and I got lucky. And I believe that luck can be created. To me, that's an equation, luck equals to opportunity plus preparation plus action. So the first thing is you need opportunities. So do lucky people have more opportunities than unlucky people? Yes. And the reason is because see, opportunities never look like opportunities. Opportunities always come disguised as problems. And we all have problems. So, in other words, we all have opportunities disguised. But it takes a lucky person to see the opportunity disguised as a problem.
我知道运气在生活中的成功中起着重要作用。人们如何能鼓励运气呢？好吧。如果你听很多人说，他们会说我很幸运，我很幸运，我很幸运。我相信运气是可以创造的。对我来说，这是一种公式：运气=机会+准备+行动。因此，首先你需要机会。那么，幸运的人是否比不幸的人拥有更多机会呢？是的。原因在于，机会从来不看起来像机会。机会总是伪装成问题。我们都有问题。换句话说，我们都有伪装的机会。但只有幸运的人才能看到伪装成问题的机会。

And that can be learned. That's a shift of your paradigm. That's a shift of your mindset. So, for example, when I was young, again, my problem was that I was in a lousy class. I was a lousy student. And I always asked myself, why did this happen to me? Why can't I be a smart student? But at one stage I then said, hey, that problem is an opportunity. Because now I can write a book to share with people how a dumb person like me could top the university, and that's how it gave birth to the book I'm Gifted, So Are You. See, if I was smart all the way, I couldn't write that book. I'm Gifted So Are You. There's no credibility  give it back to you, right? So that was an opportunity. The second thing was, I was prepared. In other words, you got to have, you've got to be prepared to take advantage of the opportunities. So, if I was not prepared with the ability to write that book, if I was not prepared with the skills on how to promote and to sell that book, it would not have been a successful book. So always ensure you upgrade your skills so you have the internal resources, the creativity, the communication skills, the management skills to take advantage of the opportunities when you see them. And the third thing is the ability to get yourself to take that first step, to take action. because many people I know see the opportunity, they say I know what to do, I know how to do it, I never did it. Because they suffer from paralysis of analysis. What if I fail? People always ask, what if I fail? I look at them and ask them, what if you succeed?
这可以被学习。这是一个思维方式的转变，是范式的转变。例如，当我年轻的时候，我的问题是我在一个差的班级里，我是一个糟糕的学生。我总是问自己，为什么会发生这种事？我为什么不能成为一个聪明的学生？但在某个阶段，我说，嘿，那问题就是一个机会。因为现在我可以写一本书，分享一个像我这样笨的人如何在大学中获得第一名的故事，这就是我写下《我有天赋，你也有》这本书的起源。你看，如果我一直都很聪明，我就无法写那本书《我有天赋，你也有》。没有信誉可言，对吧？所以那是一个机会。第二点是，我已经做好了准备。换句话说，你必须准备好去利用机会。因此，如果我没有准备好写那本书的能力，如果我没有准备好推广和销售那本书的技能，那它就不会成为一本成功的书。因此，要始终确保你提升自己的技能，这样当你看到机会时，你就有内部资源、创造力、沟通技能和管理技能去利用它们。第三点是你必须能够迈出第一步，采取行动。因为我认识的很多人看到机会时，会说我知道该怎么做，我知道如何去做，但我从未去做。因为他们遭受分析麻痹的困扰。人们总是问，如果我失败了呢？我看着他们问，假如你成功呢？

Think about that, right? To me, when you take action, you always get results. You either get results you want or results you don't want, but you always get results. And if you take action and you get results you don't want, at least you learned something from it. You're better than someone else who talked and talked and thought and thought and thought but didn't do anything at all. So just take action, because you can't fail unless you don't learn something from it. Adam, I can't thank you enough for this great interview, and this is terrific. It's been a pleasure. Thank you so much.
考虑一下，对吧？对我来说，当你采取行动时，你总会得到结果。你要么得到你想要的结果，要么得到你不想要的结果，但你总会得到结果。如果你采取行动并得到不想要的结果，至少你从中学到了什么。你比那些只是谈论、思考却什么也不做的人要好得多。因此，只需采取行动，因为除非你从中学到东西，否则你就不会失败。亚当，非常感谢你这次精彩的访谈，真是太棒了。非常高兴能与你交流。谢谢你！



### Optional Bonus Video: Nelson Dellis Memory Tips #2

Hello again. Welcome. My name is Nelson. And in this video, we are gonna talk about how to memorize a grocery list, something that we have to do every day, almost every day; at least some type of list we have to memorize every day. And a grocery list is one of those items. So to memorize a list of things, we can use different techniques, but the best one, the one that memory champions use in competition to do these crazy things, is called the memory palace. But first, we need to decide what our list is. Now, you could just memorize the list by going through all these items in your head over and over again,but that's boring. That's the way you did it in preschool and kindergarten and first grade, sixth grade, high school. And it took you hours, and you hated it. The easy way is using this memory palace technique. Taking this list and putting it in a familiar place like your apartment or your house, your workplace, anything you know really well that you can navigate in your mind's eye. So what you do is you take yourself back to that place and you imagine those pieces of your grocery list along a path through that place. Now, it's up to you what to do with those images that you're going to put in the place. The more bizarre, out of the ordinary, crazy you make these pictures, the more you're gonna remember them. So try to make them as silly as possible. Don't understand what I mean quite yet? I'm going to show you. Let's dive into my mind and actually place these items on my grocery list around my apartment. Let's go. You ready? So as you can see, it's pretty easy to memorize any list as long as you just place those crazy images of whatever you're trying to memorize in a location. The idea is that when you go back to remember what you memorized - you're in the grocery store, you're trying to think of that list - all you have to do is mentally go back to that same place in your head where you stored them and walk back through, picking up the images that you laid on the floor, in the sink, in the bathtub, all along that same - very same path. Cool, right? The best thing about it - you can do that forwards, you can do that backwards. I could tell you what the fifth item was, six item was, all I have to do is jump to that location on my mind. And that is the memory palace. You can memorize thousands of digits, tons of packs of cards, all the presidents, every winner of the NFL Super Bowl, whatever you want, you can use the memory palace to memorize. I have no doubt in my mind that your memory will be awesome by the time you're done with it. I'll see you on the flip side as a memory champion.
你好，再次欢迎。我的名字是尼尔森。在这个视频中，我们将讨论如何记住一个购物清单，这几乎是我们每天都需要做的事情；至少每天我们都需要记住某种类型的清单。购物清单就是其中之一。为了记住一系列东西，我们可以使用不同的技巧，但最好的技巧，就是记忆冠军在比赛中使用的“记忆宫殿”技术。不过首先，我们需要决定我们的清单是什么。

现在，你可以通过在脑海中一遍又一遍地回顾这些项目来记住清单，但这很无聊。这是你在学前班、幼儿园、一年级、六年级和高中时所做的。这样做需要几个小时，你肯定不喜欢。简单的方法是使用这个记忆宫殿技术。将清单放在一个熟悉的地方，比如你的公寓、房子、工作场所，或者任何你非常熟悉的地方，这样你就可以在脑海中导航。

你所要做的是回到那个地方，并想象你的购物清单的各个项目沿着一条路径出现在那个地方。至于你要如何处理这些图像，完全取决于你。你越是让这些图像显得古怪、离谱、疯狂，你就越容易记住它们。所以尽量让它们变得尽可能搞笑。还不明白我的意思？我来给你展示一下。让我们一起深入我的思维，实际上在我的公寓里放置这些购物清单的项目。准备好了吗？

正如你所看到的，只要你将这些疯狂的图像放在一个地方，记住任何清单都是非常简单的。这个方法的核心是，当你回到购物时，想起你记住的东西时——比如你在商店里，试图回想那个清单——你只需在脑海中回到你存放它们的地方，沿着同一条路径走回去，捡起你放在地板上、洗碗池里、浴缸里的图像。这很酷，对吧？最棒的是——你可以正着走，也可以反着走。我可以告诉你第五个项目是什么，第六个项目是什么，我所要做的就是跳到我脑海中的那个位置。这就是记忆宫殿。你可以记住成千上万的数字、无数副扑克牌、所有的总统、每一届NFL超级碗的获胜者，随你所愿，你都可以使用记忆宫殿进行记忆。我毫不怀疑，等你完成时，你的记忆将会非常出色。再见，我们记忆冠军再见。



### 3-1 Week 3 Introduction

If you're like most people, your career will play, is playing or has played an important role in your life, but how much should personal passions come in to play regarding what you're doing either for your career or even for fun. How can you approach your learning strategically, So you can both benefit from and enjoy what you're doing? How can you handle push back if you want to change in ways that others around you may not expect? What if you have a career catastrophe? All of these questions, and more, will be explored this week in Mind Shift.
如果你像大多数人一样，你的职业在你的生活中扮演着重要角色，但个人热情在你从事的工作或休闲活动中应该占据多大比例？你如何以战略性的方法进行学习，以便从中受益并享受你所做的事情？如果你想以他人可能不太预期的方式进行改变，如何应对反对意见？如果你遇到职业上的灾难，该怎么办？这一周的《思维转变》中将探讨所有这些问题，以及更多内容。



### 3-2 Passion and Work Part 1

We often face real challenges in our life between what we want to do, our passion and what kinds of opportunities there are out there in the working world. Let's take me, for example, as a young person. I had an absolute passion to study linguistics and to learn another language. Like many young people, I was a little headstrong. My father, on the other hand, kept saying, you can't easily get a job in linguistics. He nudged me towards learning something science-based. After all, he had had a great career as a veterinarian. I couldn't afford to go to the university on my own back then. College loans weren't easily available, but there was one way to learn the language and actually get paid for it and that was to join the army. That's why at 18, I began studying Russian at the Defense Language Institute. I was convinced that my father was wrong. And somehow, I'd find a great career for myself doing what I loved, but that's also how I found myself at age 26 in a career dead end.
我们常常面临生活中的真正挑战，即我们想做的事情、我们的激情与外面工作世界的机会之间的冲突。以我自己为例，作为年轻人，我对学习语言学和掌握另一种语言充满热情。像许多年轻人一样，我有点固执。我的父亲则不断说，语言学的工作不容易找。他鼓励我去学习一些与科学相关的专业。毕竟，他作为兽医有着很好的职业生涯。那时候，我无法自己负担上大学的费用，大学贷款也不容易获得，但有一种方法可以学习语言并且还可以获得报酬，那就是加入军队。这就是为什么在18岁时，我开始在国防语言学院学习俄语。我坚信我父亲是错的，想要找到一份做自己喜欢的工作的好职业，但这也是我在26岁时陷入职业困境的原因。

Although the military taught me a lot, when I decided to leave the military and return to the civilian world, I discovered I'd inadvertently put myself in a sort of trap. There wasn't a lot of call for people whose only professional skill was the ability to speak Russian and who knew little else. Much as I love the Russian language, I had put my focus on developing one single skill without thinking about how much that skill was really needed in the working world and without thinking about whether other skills might complement and enhance my ability to get the kinds of jobs I wanted to have. This is part of what I call the Passion Trap. We're often encouraged to follow our passions by well meaning people, friends and teachers, especially who don't themselves have to suffer the consequences of long term difficulties in getting a job. Friends after all, often want to make you happy right now. So, they'll often tell you what they think you want to hear. Teachers have a job teaching about their passion. This means that they benefit from encouraging you to take the classes and even aim towards their professions even if the chances of you actually getting a job related to that profession are minimal. On the other hand, parents, much like my father are often only focused on your finding a successful career. They can be less concerned about what you feel are your internal passions, especially if they, themselves have had a difficult life and they know how hard it can be to make a comfortable living. This push and pull between our internal passions, and the needs of the working world isn't something that just relates to young people. We often feel these forces throughout our lives. There are internal desires, the external needs of the world and many different influences from our family, our friends and our teachers and mentors. There is no one single answer to all this, but there are thoughtful ways to address this challenge as you think about your career and your approach to life long learning. Thinking visually about your talents can be helpful. That's what we'll cover in the next video.
虽然军队教会了我很多东西，但当我决定离开军队，回到平民生活时，我发现自己不知不觉中陷入了一种困境。仅仅掌握俄语这一项专业技能的人并不多，市场需求也不大。尽管我热爱俄语，但我将注意力集中在发展这项单一技能上，却没有考虑到这项技能在工作世界中的实际需求，也没有考虑到其他技能是否可以补充和增强我获得所希望工作的能力。这就是我所称的“激情陷阱”的一部分。我们常常受到好意的朋友和老师的鼓励，让我们追随自己的激情，尤其是那些不必承受长期找工作困难后果的人。毕竟，朋友们通常希望让你现在感到快乐，因此他们常常会告诉你他们认为你想听的话。老师们则是因为对自己所热爱的领域有了解，他们的工作就是教导这个领域。因此，他们鼓励你上他们的课，甚至朝着他们的职业方向努力，即使你实际上获得与该职业相关的工作的机会微乎其微。另一方面，像我父亲那样的父母，通常只关注你找到一份成功的职业。他们可能对你内心的激情不太关心，尤其是当他们自己经历过艰难的生活，并知道谋生有多么困难时。这种内心激情与外部工作需求之间的拉锯，不仅仅是年轻人面临的问题。在我们生活的整个过程中，我们常常会感受到这些力量。有内心的渴望、外部世界的需求以及来自家庭、朋友和老师、导师的各种不同影响。对此并没有一个单一的答案，但在你思考自己的职业和终身学习方法时，有一些深思熟虑的方式可以应对这一挑战。通过视觉化你的才能来思考是很有帮助的。接下来的视频中，我们将讨论这一点。



### 3-3 Passion and Work Part 2

Most people think about their career development as taking the form of a sort of a T. So you have your arms out, and the T going down. In other words, you have one heavy-duty skill, that's the downward part of the T, and you complement it by taking some superficial knowledge of other things. That's the initial approach I took to my career. I learned Russian, and also learned a smattering of other skills, like how to type, how to drive  a truck. The challenge of course, is that I found myself without too many opportunities. But there's another way to think about careers. That's the pi approach, which is promoted by Patrick Tay, an elected member of Singapore's Parliament. Notice that this career approach has sort of two legs, gives you more balance, right? And you have one main skill, say accounting, but you also want to supplement that with knowledge in another area, say counselling. The second area may be directly related or it may be quite different from the first. If time and money are tight, you should try to build your second skill out of what you're already familiar with. When I went to look at second skilling myself, I took a clue from what I'd witnessed in the military. Having at least some technical competence in your skills toolkit often means you have more opportunities. So that was a big push for me towards getting a second set of skills in engineering. Even though I didn't think I had any passion or talent for engineering. To my surprise, when I began getting better at my engineering studies, I began to realize I liked engineering and I found something more. My previous background as a linguist actually enhanced my studies of engineering and my ability as engineer. I'd learned about chunking and interleaving and deliberate practice. In other words, I'd learned how to learn. I thought more creatively about my engineering studies because of my passion for language. There are many examples of people becoming successful at their passion only because they stopped focusing directly and solely on that passion, and instead began incorporating real world considerations. For example, writer Scott Turow initially had trouble making it as an author. So he took a step sideways instead to attend law school. The real world expertise he acquired as a lawyer gave his fiction extraordinary power. His books have since sold more than 30 million copies around the world. As you know, my hero in science is the father of modern neuroscience, Santiago Ramon y Cajal. Cajal's father was a doctor who pushed his son hard towards becoming a doctor, but Cajal himself wanted to be an artist. Here it was, Spain in the 1860s, and the arguments between a parent and child were the same as they are today. Cajal's father pointed out that it was almost impossible to make a living as an artist but Cajal resisted strongly. Until, that is, Cajal finally realized that the real world is important. In fact, he was going nowhere fast. Finally, he began turning his attention towards working to become a doctor. It was very difficult for him. He flunked some major examinations, but he kept trying. However, he never forgot his passion for art. In fact, he brought that artistic passion into his study of medicine which ultimately played an important role in helping Cajal win the Nobel Prize. So remember, you can bring a second skill into your work because of your passion, or simply because it enhances or complements your first skill. You may have to spend some parts of your life focusing on one thing in order to get deep skilling in that area, but you don't have to give up on your passion. In fact, your passion can greatly enhance your creative ability in your other skill. In the end, it's never a good idea to just blindly follow your passion. In fact, look at the real world and work to both follow and broaden your passions. Your life will be greatly enriched.
大多数人认为职业发展可以用一个“T”形来描述。所以你有双臂伸展，而“T”向下延伸。换句话说，你拥有一项重大的技能，这就是“T”的竖线部分，然后你通过对其他事情的肤浅知识来补充它。这是我当初对职业的初步理解。我学习了俄语，同时也掌握了一些其他技能，比如打字和驾驶卡车。当然，挑战在于，我发现自己没有太多的机会。但还有另一种思考职业的方式，那就是“π”形的方式，这种方式是新加坡国会议员Patrick Tay所提倡的。注意，这种职业方法有两个支撑，更加平衡，对吧？你有一项主要技能，比如会计，但你还想补充另一领域的知识，比如咨询。第二个领域可能与第一个领域直接相关，也可能与第一个领域大相径庭。如果时间和金钱紧张，你应该尽量利用自己已有的知识来培养第二项技能。当我考虑第二项技能时，我从在军队时的经历中得到了启示。拥有一些技术能力的技能工具包通常意味着你会有更多机会。因此，这促使我朝着工程方面的第二技能发展。尽管我当时认为自己没有对工程的激情或天赋。令我惊讶的是，当我开始在工程学习中取得进步时，我意识到我喜欢工程，并发现了更多。我的语言学背景实际上增强了我对工程的学习和作为工程师的能力。我学会了分块、交错学习和刻意练习。换句话说，我学会了如何学习。因为我对语言的热爱，我在工程学习中更加创造性地思考。

许多成功人士的例子表明，他们之所以能够在自己的激情中取得成功，恰恰是因为他们不再仅仅专注于那种激情，而是开始融入现实世界的考量。例如，作家Scott Turow起初在成为作家方面遇到了困难。因此，他选择了横向发展，去上法学院。他作为律师所获得的现实世界经验赋予了他的小说非凡的力量。他的书籍至今在全球售出超过3000万本。如你所知，我心目中的科学英雄是现代神经科学之父，Santiago Ramon y Cajal。Cajal的父亲是一位医生，他强迫儿子走上医生的道路，但Cajal自己却想成为一名艺术家。在19世纪60年代的西班牙，父母与孩子之间的争论和今天一样。Cajal的父亲指出，作为艺术家几乎不可能谋生，但Cajal坚决反对。直到Cajal最终意识到，现实世界是重要的。实际上，他毫无进展。最后，他开始将注意力转向成为医生。对他来说，这非常困难。他在一些重要考试中不及格，但他不断努力。然而，他从未忘记对艺术的热爱。事实上，他将这种艺术热情带入了医学研究中，这最终在帮助Cajal赢得诺贝尔奖方面发挥了重要作用。

所以请记住，你可以将第二项技能融入工作中，无论是因为你的激情，还是因为它增强或补充了你的第一项技能。你可能需要在生活的某些阶段专注于一件事，以便在该领域深耕，但你不必放弃自己的激情。事实上，你的激情可以极大地增强你在其他技能方面的创造力。最终，盲目追随你的激情从来都不是一个好主意。实际上，审视现实世界，努力同时追求和拓宽你的激情，这样你的生活将会大大丰富。



### 3-4 Passion and Work Part 3

In the last video we talked about careers and skills as being either t-shaped, with only one deep skill, or pi-shaped with two areas of emphasis. But of course there are other ways to think about careers and skills and don't forget that hobbies can also play a role in your life of learning. Not do they make you happy, they help keep your brain fresh and agile. Sometimes they can even end up enhancing your career. For example, one of my hobbies is to watch a bit of television in the evenings with my husband, Phil. And this help me develop insights over the years about how the video medium looks and works, which in turn has helped me to build better MOOCs.
在上一个视频中，我们讨论了职业和技能可以被视为“T”型，只有一项深厚的技能，或者“π”型，具有两个重点领域。当然，还有其他方式可以看待职业和技能，也不要忘记爱好在你的学习生活中也能发挥作用。爱好不仅能让你快乐，还能帮助你的大脑保持活力和灵活。有时，它们甚至可能增强你的职业发展。

例如，我的一个爱好是在晚上和我的丈夫Phil一起看一些电视节目。多年来，这帮助我对视频媒介的外观和运作方式发展了一些见解，这反过来又帮助我建立了更好的MOOC课程。

But look at how other people think about building their skill sets. Scott Adams, who's the creator of the famous Dilbert cartoon, points out that he's got mediocre skills in a lot of areas. He's a second grade artist, with reasonable writing, business, marketing, and social media skills. Put all those middling skills together, however, and it becomes clearer why Adams has been so successful as a cartoonist. His overall talent stack is terrific, even if he's not particularly good at any one area.
但是看看其他人是如何看待构建他们的技能组合的。著名的《迪尔伯特》漫画创作者斯科特·亚当斯指出，他在很多领域的技能都很普通。他的绘画水平一般，但在写作、商业、市场营销和社交媒体方面有一定的能力。然而，将这些平庸的技能结合在一起，就更能清楚地看出为什么亚当斯作为漫画家如此成功。他的整体技能组合非常出色，即使他在任何一个领域都不是特别优秀。

Many individuals focus on acquiring a specific skill, say, a certain programming language. But they forget that other skills, such as being able to speak humorously and effectively, can add formidable value to their talents stack. US sales entrepreneur Rodney Grim for example, keeps his focus on his broad profession in selling electronics. As he points out. I'm a jack of all trades. While this limits me from truly excelling at one thing in particular. It also serves as a strong defense in a technological world where the rate of change is only accelerated. I've been an electronics technician, a programmer, a salesman. I also own my own business. And I shift my roles drawing on my background as opportunity and change dictate.
许多人专注于掌握某项特定技能，比如某种编程语言。但他们忘记了其他技能，比如幽默而有效的沟通能力，可以为他们的技能组合增加强大的价值。例如，美国销售企业家罗德尼·格里姆专注于自己在电子产品销售方面的广泛职业。正如他所指出的：“我是一个万事通。虽然这限制了我在某一特定领域真正出类拔萃，但在技术变化日益加速的世界中，这也成为了我的强大防御。我曾是一名电子技术员、一名程序员、一名销售员。我还拥有自己的企业，并根据机遇和变化调整我的角色。”

Brian Brookshire who's worked as an online marketing specialist, looks at second-skilling from a related perspective.
布赖恩·布鲁克希尔（Brian Brookshire）曾担任在线营销专家，他从相关的角度看待第二技能的提升。

To tell the truth, often there really isn't that much difference between someone who's been on the job for six months and someone who's been working that same job for six years. So second skilling doesn't need to be as difficult as you might think.
说实话，通常在同一份工作工作六个月的人和工作六年的人之间并没有太大的差别。因此，第二技能的提升并不像你想象的那么困难。

Skill development careers are typically logarithmic and not linear. Which means that, while developing deep expertise may take a long time, often, you can rapidly accelerate to the point of diminishing returns in a fairly short period of time. And this is often good enough to get a toehold in a new area. Personally, I find that I really enjoy requiring lots of new skills because of that thrill you get with the initial rush of progress.
技能发展的职业通常是对数型的，而不是线性的。这意味着，虽然培养深厚的专业知识可能需要很长时间，但通常，你可以在相对较短的时间内迅速加速到收益递减的点。而这往往足以让你在一个新领域立足。就我个人而言，我发现自己非常享受学习大量新技能，因为那种初步进展带来的兴奋感让我感到很快乐。

Sometimes you might find yourself blocked when you're aiming for a certain career. For example, Princess Allotey, couldn't afford to go full time to the university to study the mathematics she loved. So I intend to give back to my community. I volunteered as a math teaching assistant, and I taught kids math in Ghana. I certainly proved language can improve things for kids in Ghana. And I ended up going around Ghana making presentations. Surprisingly, I developed this skill what I always wanted to do enough, and that was public speaking. Intishar Rashad from Bangladesh has also made the most of a startling change of fortune. When I graduated from high school, I decided to go into the military to become an air force engineer. However, due to an accident, I suffered a severe spine injury and it seemed to ruin my potential career choice. Instead of losing hope, I changed my mindset and now I'm a medical student focusing on a career in medicine. So if you're blocked, either temporarily or permanently in what you want to learn or do, that's often a great opportunity to second skill yourself, or do something else that's equally exciting or fulfilling. Once you started learning the new skill, you'll often be surprised to see the powerful enhancement it makes with relation to your preexisting skills. And remember, non-academic topics can be invaluable assets to your career. For example, Singapore entrepreneur, Adam Koo, found that his skills in magic And in DJing, completely unrelated to his degree in business, have taught him a lot about how to effectively engage with audiences. The result, he now runs one of Southeast Asia's largest private educational institutions training to tens of thousands each year. In the end, it's always important to keep your mind open and to keep learning. This is the best way to ensure your skills don't become obsolete. Read, take MOOCS, and take courses and seminars to keep yourself prepared, no matter what twists or turns your career may take. Do you have a skill or hobby that's been overlooked but that could be valuable? Are there new technical areas you could start now to gradually learn about that you've previously dismissed as being something you wouldn't be able to do? Head on over to the discussion forum and let us know about some of your hidden talent, potential and desires. And get ideas from the hidden talent and potential of others.
有时，当你朝着某个职业目标努力时，可能会发现自己遇到了障碍。例如，Princess Allotey因为负担不起全日制上大学学习自己热爱的数学而感到困扰。于是，她决定回馈社区，担任数学助教，教孩子们数学。我确实证明了语言可以改善加纳孩子们的学习。我还在加纳各地进行演讲。出乎意料的是，我发展了我一直想做的技能，那就是公共演讲。来自孟加拉国的Intishar Rashad也在突如其来的命运变化中充分发挥了自己的潜力。高中毕业时，我决定参军，成为一名空军工程师。然而，由于一次事故，我遭受了严重的脊椎损伤，这似乎毁了我的职业选择。面对这样的困境，我没有失去希望，而是改变了心态，现在我是一名医学生，专注于医学事业。

因此，如果你在想学习或做的事情上暂时或永久地受到阻碍，这往往是一个很好的机会来提升第二技能，或去做其他同样令人兴奋或有成就感的事情。一旦你开始学习新技能，通常会惊讶地发现它对你现有技能的强大增强效果。并且请记住，非学术主题也可以成为你职业生涯中宝贵的资产。例如，新加坡企业家Adam Koo发现，他在魔术和DJ方面的技能，与他商业学位完全无关，却教会了他如何有效地与观众互动。结果，他现在运营着东南亚最大的私立教育机构之一，每年培训数万名学生。

最后，始终保持开放的心态和不断学习是非常重要的。这是确保你的技能不会过时的最佳方式。阅读、参加MOOC、参加课程和研讨会，以便随时做好准备，无论你的职业生涯经历怎样的曲折。你是否有被忽视的技能或爱好，但它可能会很有价值？是否有你以前认为自己做不到的新技术领域可以现在开始逐步学习？前往讨论论坛，告诉我们你的一些隐藏才能、潜力和愿望，并从他人的隐藏才能和潜力中获取灵感。



### 3-5 Mindshifting – What to Do in the Face of Opposition

One tough challenge is deciding when young people should be directed towards a specific career, because this decision can have reverberations that can last throughout people's lives. In some parts of the world, students are sorted into career paths early on. At age 16, for example, they may be sent to either vocational training for the skilled trades or towards more academically oriented training. In other parts of the world, this choice is sometimes delayed. There are advantages and disadvantages to each of these approaches. People choose career paths for all sorts of reasons. In some countries, the parents often make the choice, regardless of what their kids want to do. In other countries, the students themselves often make the choice, despite the fact that they may have almost no real world experience with the job choice they're making. Or sometimes, people simply come from a background where they've had no previous access to quality education or even to any proper education at all, which means that their career choices are limited from the outset.
一个艰难的挑战是决定年轻人何时应该被引导向特定的职业，因为这个决定可能会对人们的生活产生长远的影响。在世界某些地方，学生很早就被分配到职业道路上。例如，在16岁时，他们可能被送往职业培训以学习技术工种，或者接受更学术导向的培训。在世界其他地方，这一选择有时会被推迟。这两种方法各有优缺点。

人们选择职业道路的原因多种多样。在一些国家，父母常常做出选择，而不管孩子们想做什么。在其他国家，学生们则通常自己做出选择，尽管他们对所做职业选择几乎没有任何实际的工作经验。有时，人们来自的背景也可能意味着他们之前没有接受过优质教育，甚至没有接受过任何适当的教育，这意味着他们的职业选择一开始就受到限制。

Or people can be on a very wisely chosen career path but then once they're exposed to new opportunities and insights, they may want to change. Career change, and change of all kinds, is easier to do in some countries and cultures than others. And, of course, it can be easier to jump from some disciplines than others, age is also a factor. But as you probably gathered, my own sense is that well thought out career change, and change of any kind, whether a small shift to acquire a different set of skills that enhance your abilities to do your job within your company, or a major shift to a new career. Forms of vitally important, creative fuel for all societies. One of the biggest hurdles to changing career paths or a change of any sort can be well meaning friends, parents, and colleagues. It's not like this sort of push back from others is necessarily a bad thing. It makes you consider your choice very carefully. One important rule of thumb, is to avoid going into debt while learning new skills at the field you're hoping to move into is poorly paid. There's something very wrong in spending a large amount to acquire a new knowledge or new skills, only to be poorly paid when you ultimately get out on the job. If you are considering career change or even simple second skilling, here are a few tips for dealing with the push back from others, who might want you to stay the way you are. With the dabble approach, you simply start gradually learning in the new area, either online, through reading or by taking local classes. This is a slow approach. But it can also help ensure that you, yourself, can gradually grow with the change, which will make the transition less jarring for all involved. The double life approach is much more intense than dabbling. With this approach, you basically compartmentalize your life and avoid talking to people about what you're trying to do. This can be a more stressful way to tackle your change, but it can have an advantage. It can prevent others from trying to talk you out of your goals because you'll appear to be continuing just as usual. For example, you may continue working as a musician while you're taking side courses to prepare you for a career in health care. And then there's being a contrarian. Take pride in being a contrarian. The more others say you will fail, the more it can help bolster your internal resolve. Keep in mind, however, that it's important to choose reachable and doable interim goals and check points to assess your progress. For example, if you tried as hard as you can, but repeatedly get very low scores on the test to get into medical school, it maybe time to reassess your dream of going to medical school. And don't forget that who you are is not just you.
或者，人们可能处于一个非常明智选择的职业道路上，但一旦接触到新的机会和见解，他们可能会想要改变。职业变更，以及各种变化，在一些国家和文化中比其他地方更容易。当然，从某些学科跳槽比其他学科更容易，年龄也是一个因素。但是，正如你可能已经意识到的，我个人认为，经过深思熟虑的职业变更，以及任何形式的变化，无论是为了获得一组不同的技能以增强你在公司内部工作的能力的小转变，还是向新职业的大幅转变，都是所有社会中至关重要的创造性燃料。

改变职业道路或任何形式变化的最大障碍之一可能是出于好意的朋友、父母和同事。来自他人的这种阻力并不一定是坏事。它使你非常仔细地考虑自己的选择。一个重要的经验法则是，避免在学习新技能时产生债务，尤其是当你希望进入的领域薪水较低时。在花费大量资金获取新知识或新技能后，最终工作时却得不到良好的报酬，这显然是有问题的。

如果你正在考虑职业变更甚至简单的第二技能提升，以下是一些应对他人推阻的建议，他们可能希望你保持现状。通过“试探法”，你可以逐渐在新领域学习，无论是在线学习、阅读还是参加当地课程。这是一种缓慢的方法，但它也可以帮助确保你自己能够逐渐适应变化，这将使所有相关人员的过渡变得不那么突兀。

而“双重生活法”则比试探法更为激烈。通过这种方法，你基本上把生活分开，并避免与他人谈论你正在尝试做的事情。这可能是一种更具压力的方式来应对变化，但它也有一个优势。它可以防止他人试图劝说你放弃目标，因为你会显得一切照常进行。例如，你可能继续作为音乐工作，同时参加副课程为进入医疗行业做好准备。

最后，还有“逆反者”策略。为成为逆反者感到自豪。别人越是说你会失败，越能增强你的内在决心。然而，请记住，选择可实现的、可行的中期目标和检查点以评估你的进展是很重要的。例如，如果你已经尽全力，但在医学院入学考试中反复获得很低的分数，那么是时候重新评估你进入医学院的梦想了。别忘了，你的身份不仅仅是你自己。

Who you are also depends on your environment. This means, that by changing your environment, you can speed up the process of mind shifting. I shifted from physics to biology by immersing myself in the best neuroscience environment I could find. I picked up a lot of facts, but much more important, was what I learned by osmosis without conscious awareness of what it was I was learning. I learned how to think like a biologists, by being around biologists and interacting with them. I did make a conscious effort not to fall back on what I had been, a physicist and mindset and skills of a physics. I took a vow of physics poverty to remain open to what was new around me rather than revert back to the old thought patterns. This approach also works for learning a new language, you get to observe the culture along with the language.
你是谁也取决于你的环境。这意味着，通过改变环境，你可以加速思维转变的过程。我通过沉浸在我能找到的最佳神经科学环境中，从物理学转向生物学。我掌握了很多事实，但更重要的是，我在无意识的情况下通过渗透学习到了很多东西。我通过与生物学家在一起并与他们互动，学会了像生物学家一样思考。我确实有意识地努力不让自己回到物理学家的思维方式和技能上。我发誓要放弃物理学的贫困，以保持对周围新事物的开放，而不是回归旧的思维模式。这种方法对学习一门新语言也适用，你可以在学习语言的同时观察文化。

In your attempts at career change, you don't want to minimize important considerations. Like whether you've got at least the basics of what it might take to succeed. Be willing to solicit and listen to valid criticism about how you can change and improve. You don't want to be like the cluelessly bad karaoke singer, warbling haplessly into the night because his friends always told him he was great. If you are a friend, parent, or mentor, of a potential mind shifter, try your best to remain open to other people's ability to change. And if you're the one who's making the change yourself, count yourself lucky if those around you are supportive, and use the opportunity to enjoy your new learning path.
在你尝试职业转变时，不要忽视一些重要的考虑因素，比如你是否具备成功所需的基本条件。愿意征求并倾听关于你如何改变和改进的有效批评是很重要的。你不想成为那个 clueless 的糟糕卡拉OK歌手，傻傻地在夜晚唱着，因为他的朋友们总是告诉他他唱得很好。如果你是一个潜在的思维转变者的朋友、父母或导师，尽量对其他人改变的能力保持开放态度。如果你是自己进行改变的人，如果身边的人支持你，那你就要感到幸运，并利用这个机会享受你新的学习之路。


### 3-6 General Competence versus Selective Ignorance

If you have long term goals in a difficult to master area, one of the best things you can do is to immerse yourself in what you're learning. For example, if you're planning to become successful in the restaurant business, one of the best things you can do is to get experience in every aspect of restauranting that you possibly can, from busing tables, to serving, to managing accounts. Without this kind of experience, it can be a lot easier to make mistakes that allow your future business to fail. This may seem obvious, but sometimes the cockiness that helps fuel and, results from our success in one area can go to our heads. Even eminent scientists, for example, have been known to fail disastrously when they tried to jump into a new area without getting themselves properly prepared. My co-instructor, Terry Sejnowski, for example, took these ideas into account when he switched from the study of physics to the study of neuroscience. I was advised to get neurons under my fingernails. I worked hard over years to master the biology I needed to truly understand the new discipline I was moving into. At the same time, I practiced selective ignorance. I knew that my expertise with computers, a rare asset in the late 1970s, could mean that I'd be dragged into computer related work that would keep me away from the biology I needed to master. So I vowed not to touch a computer during those years, giving me time to focus on the biology that I needed to master. Selective ignorance, then, is another important career tip. You want to master all the details that you can that will support you in what you're trying to learn or do. But at the same time, you don't want to simply start being used by other people as a tool for their own work. Marketing specialist, Bryan Brookshire, has some additional insight along these lines. I told a former boss that I wanted to learn how to do everything at the company and her reply was, don't do that. You've got to cultivate selective ignorance because if you know how to do everything, then you become everybody's go to person and that can interfere with getting your own work done, and that turned out to be pretty good advice. Cultivating selective ignorance has often prevented me from getting drafted into projects that I had no interest in participating in, or time for.
如果你在一个难以掌握的领域有长期目标，最好的做法之一就是全身心投入到你所学习的内容中。例如，如果你计划在餐饮业取得成功，最好的方法之一就是尽可能多地积累餐饮各个方面的经验，从清理餐桌、服务，到管理账目。如果没有这种经验，你可能更容易犯错误，导致未来的生意失败。这听起来很明显，但有时，我们在某个领域的成功所带来的自负会让我们变得傲慢。例如，著名科学家在跳入新领域而没有做好充分准备时，往往会遭遇灾难性失败。我的共同讲师特里·塞诺斯基在从物理学转向神经科学的过程中，就考虑到了这些因素。我被建议要“让神经元在我的指甲下留下印记”。我努力花了多年时间掌握我需要的生物学知识，以真正理解我所转入的新学科。与此同时，我也练习选择性无知。我知道，自己在1970年代末期对计算机的专长可能会让我被拉入与计算机相关的工作，这会妨碍我专注于需要掌握的生物学。因此，我发誓在那几年不碰计算机，给自己留出时间专注于需要掌握的生物学。因此，选择性无知是另一个重要的职业建议。你要掌握所有能支持你学习或工作的细节，但同时，不要让自己成为他人工作中的工具。市场营销专家布莱恩·布鲁克希尔对此有一些额外的见解。他告诉我，一位前老板对他说他想学会公司里的所有工作，而她的回应是：“不要这样做。你得培养选择性无知，因为如果你知道如何做所有事情，你就会成为每个人的首选，这会干扰你自己的工作。”这条建议证明是非常好的。培养选择性无知常常让我避免参与那些我没有兴趣或没有时间参与的项目。

So there you have it, general competence, along with selective ignorance are two important keys for career success.
所以，综合能力和选择性无知是职业成功的两个重要关键。



### 3-7 The Value of Feeling Like an Imposter

The imposter syndrome is that feeling that you're not as good or as talented as the other people around you. It's actually a very common feeling, especially if you're venturing into a new or different area. Often, feeling like an imposter makes you afraid that you won't be able to succeed at whatever tasks lay before you. After all, you think, if everyone around you is somehow more talented or knowledgeable, what chance do you have to succeed? These feelings can make the tasks ahead of you seem even more formidable and difficult. Your mind tells you, you only got to where you are because of good luck, and you suspect that good luck might not be enough to continue to propel yourself forward to success. Psychologists often say that feeling like an imposter is a bad thing, and you should just stop feeling like that. But here's an important point. Doubting yourself isn't always bad. It can keep you more open and flexible to seeing and doing what you need to do to succeed. And in fact, people who are open to self doubt tend to be more successful in the long run. Why is this? As it turns out, people can tend to fail, not so much from under confidence, but from overconfidence. History is filled with the stories of business executives, generals, and politicians who only listen to others when they reinforce their own convictions. These leaders then steer with blithe abandon towards disaster. Doubt, of course, can be overdone, but it can also be undervalued. In fact, if you're full of doubt, that means you have a mindset that leaves you more open to what's going on around you. It can spur you on to try harder, and as we know in this course, it's persistence and flexibility that can be what matters most in the long run, not genius. It's natural that most of us except, perhaps, the most brash and narcissistic can fall occasional pray to feeling like an imposter. Accepting that these feelings are normal and re-framing them to our advantage forms a healthy way to move forward.
冒名顶替综合症是指你感到自己不如周围其他人优秀或有才华的感觉。这实际上是一种很常见的感受，尤其是在你进入一个新的或不同的领域时。通常，感到自己像个冒名顶替者会让你担心自己无法成功完成眼前的任务。毕竟，你会想，如果你周围的每个人似乎都更有才华或知识，那么你成功的机会有多大呢？这些感觉会让你面前的任务显得更加艰巨和困难。你的内心告诉你，你之所以能走到今天，是因为运气好，而你怀疑这样的好运是否足以让你继续前进，取得成功。

心理学家通常认为，感到自己像个冒名顶替者是一件坏事，你应该停止这种感觉。但这里有一个重要的观点：怀疑自己并不总是坏事。它可以让你更加开放和灵活，去观察和做你需要做的事情，以取得成功。事实上，开放自我怀疑的人在长期来看往往更成功。这是为什么呢？事实证明，人们失败往往不是因为缺乏自信，而是因为过于自信。历史上充满了商业高管、将军和政治家的故事，他们只听取那些强化自己信念的人的意见。这些领导者就这样无所畏惧地驶向灾难。

当然，怀疑有时可能过度，但它也可能被低估。事实上，如果你充满疑虑，这意味着你有一种更开放的心态，可以更好地观察周围发生的事情。这可以激励你更加努力地尝试，正如我们在这门课程中所了解到的，持久性和灵活性在长期中往往比天才更重要。大多数人，除了那些极为自负和自恋的人，偶尔都会感到像个冒名顶替者。接受这些感觉是正常的，并将它们重新框架为有利的方式，形成了一种健康的前进方式。



### 3-8 Avoiding Career Ruts and Surviving Career Catastrophes

Wherever you are in your career path, whether young, mid-career, or even in retirement, it can help to keep your eye on the big picture of societal trends in relation to your special skills. When I was young I followed my passion into a box of having a single special skill, the ability to speak a second language. I didn't think or plan to complement that ability with other skills that could give me more flexibility in the job marketplace. We know that language and culture are important. But in today's society, technological, scientific, and mathematical literacy and expertise are of increasing importance, as well. So if you have a soft-skill area of interest, it can be a good idea to balance that with some technical or analytical skills. But likewise, if you already have sharp analytical skills, it can be a good idea to enhance your talent stack by working on your soft skills such as speaking ability or writing. On a side note, I wish I had a dollar for every older student I've had in my engineering classes, who like me, followed their passion, and spent a lot of money to get a first degree in a subject that was difficult to get a good job at. I'm not saying engineering is the only field to study, although I will admit to a little bias for engineering as good general training in today's society. But be aware how easy it can be during the career selection process to fall into a  sheeple mentality. Where you and your friends don't find out until it's too late that you've put yourself into decades of debt studying a favorite subject that's better off as a hobby than as a career. What if you get fired or laid off from a job? A valuable point to keep in mind here is what I'll call, the golden rule of career catastrophes. And that is, it is never as bad as you think it is at the time and there is always a silver lining.  Almost always as a result of being either fired or laid off, you ultimately find yourself happier in the long run. Even Pete Best, who was kicked out of the great band The Beatles, right before they went on to world fame, was able to find a wonderful silver lining in his career catastrophe. After his ousting from the band, he would go on to meet his wife, the great love of his life. Keep in mind that it's not usually a good idea to become too settled for too many years doing the same job. You can slip into a career rut that can be difficult to get out of. Even if you're doing a variety of activities for your work, your mind can still be following into the route or rut. Which means it can gently be moving towards stagnation. In any case, you may think you have the perfect career, but things can change in a heartbeat. One simple swap in management can mean an upheaval. Even great scientists like Francis Crick, the Nobel Prize winning co-discoverer of DNA made a point of changing his area of focus to keep himself fresh as he grew older. At age 60 he switched from the study of molecular biology to the study of consciousness. This is something like spending your life as a construction worker and then deciding you're going to switch to become an expert in creating great embroidery. The result, Crick's lively intellect retained its sharp ability to focus until his dying day.
无论你在职业道路上处于哪个阶段，无论是年轻人、中年人，还是退休人士，关注社会趋势与自己特长技能之间的关系都是有益的。当我年轻时，我追随自己的热情，专注于一种特殊技能——说一门外语。我没有考虑或计划用其他技能来补充这一能力，从而在就业市场上获得更多的灵活性。我们知道语言和文化非常重要，但在当今社会，技术、科学和数学素养及专业知识也越来越重要。因此，如果你对软技能领域感兴趣，结合一些技术或分析技能可能是个好主意。同样，如果你已经具备了出色的分析技能，那么通过提升你的软技能，例如口语或写作能力，来增强你的才能组合也是明智的。

顺便提一下，我真希望我能为每一位我在工程课程中遇到的老年学生赚到一美元。他们像我一样追随自己的热情，花了大量的钱获得一个难以找到好工作的学位。我并不是说工程是唯一值得学习的领域，尽管我承认对工程有一点偏见，因为它在当今社会是良好的通用培训。但要意识到，在职业选择过程中，陷入“羊群心理”的容易程度。你和你的朋友可能直到为时已晚才发现自己已经在一个更适合作为爱好的学科上投入了几十年的债务。

如果你被解雇或裁员怎么办？在这里要记住一个宝贵的观点，我称之为“职业灾难的黄金法则”。那就是：事情从来没有你当时想得那么糟糕，总会有一个积极的一面。几乎总是因为被解雇或裁员，你最终会发现自己在长期内更快乐。甚至像皮特·贝斯特这样的人，被伟大的乐队披头士在他们走向世界名声之前踢出，也能在他的职业灾难中找到美好的转机。在被乐队开除后，他遇到了自己的妻子，成为他一生的挚爱。

请记住，长时间固定在同一工作上通常不是个好主意。你可能会陷入职业低谷，难以摆脱。即使你在工作中做着各种各样的活动，你的思维也可能依然跟随进入低谷。这意味着它可能会慢慢趋向停滞。无论如何，你可能认为自己拥有完美的职业，但情况可能会瞬息万变。管理层的一次简单变动可能意味着动荡。即使是像弗朗西斯·克里克这样伟大的科学家——诺贝尔奖获得者、DNA的共同发现者，他也强调了在年龄增长时改变研究重点以保持新鲜感的重要性。在60岁时，他从分子生物学的研究转向意识的研究。这就像花一生时间做建筑工人，然后决定转行成为刺绣专家一样。结果，克里克的聪明才智在他去世的那天仍保持着敏锐的专注力。



### 3-9 Bad Traits as Best Traits


You maybe surprised to learn that some of your worst traits can sometimes be some of your best traits. This means that when you get down on yourself for some of your bad characteristics, it's a good idea to start reframing your thinking. In this video, we'll help you get started. Let's take for our first example having a poor working memory. As we've already mentioned, having a poor working memory often indicates that you're more creative. When something falls out of the slots of your working memory, something else tends to pop in. Do you have to work harder to keep up with people who have that steel trap sort of memory? Sure, but you wouldn't want to give up the joyful advantages that your creativity gives you. And of course, people with less capable working memories are more likely to see short cuts and to have conceptual breakthroughs. Poor working memory incidentally is often correlated with Attention Deficit Disorder. So if this condition is making your learning tougher for you, it's important to realize it also gives you advantages. You may argue that a strong working memory not only helps with problem solving, it also helps with getting good grades but research has shown that there's a counter correlation between school grades and creativity. In other words, sometimes the better your grades, the worse your creativity. For some reason my fellow professors who were usually the best of the best students seem to get annoyed with me when I bring up that little factoid. Maybe that's also the origin of the old saying, the A students end up working for the C students. But there's also a correlation between disagreeableness and creativity. It may simply be that disagreeable people are more willing to be brats, to throw aside that compliant deferential behavior of their more agreeable peers. Are you a contrarian? That too can serve as an advantage when everyone's telling you you just can't succeed, you're contrarian nature combined with a little bit of common sense can be just the ticket to prove them wrong. What about being a worrier? Well, as a worrier myself, I'll be the first to admit that worrying has got some unhealthy aspects to it. But anxiety can allow you to anticipate possibilities by mentally reviewing different scenarios even if they're negative. And that's not all bad. Doing a bit of worrying and then reframing your thoughts to calm your brain in the ways we've discussed earlier is a great way to go. And how about being a naive dreamer? If you're naive, it's a nice idea to partner and work with more practical people. But a little bit of naive dreaming helps keep the world moving forward on a positive note. No one would want to give that up.
你可能会惊讶地发现，自己的一些最差特质有时实际上可以变成最好的特质。这意味着，当你因为某些坏性格而对自己感到沮丧时，重新思考是个好主意。在这个视频中，我们将帮助你入门。首先以工作记忆差为例。正如我们之前提到的，工作记忆较差往往表明你更具创造力。当某些东西从你的工作记忆中消失时，其他东西往往会进入。你确实需要更加努力地跟上那些记忆力像钢铁一样坚固的人吗？当然，但你绝对不想放弃你创造力所带来的愉悦优势。当然，工作记忆较差的人更有可能看到捷径并获得概念上的突破。顺便提一下，工作记忆差通常与注意力缺陷障碍相关联。因此，如果这种情况使你的学习变得更加困难，重要的是要意识到它也给你带来了优势。

你可能会争辩说，强大的工作记忆不仅有助于解决问题，还有助于获得好成绩，但研究表明，学校成绩与创造力之间存在负相关关系。换句话说，有时你的成绩越好，创造力反而越差。出于某种原因，我的教授同事们通常是最优秀的学生，但当我提到这个小事实时，他们似乎会感到恼火。也许这也是那句老话的来源：A学生最终为C学生工作。但是，不可合作性与创造力之间也存在相关性。也许正是因为不合群的人更愿意表现得像个小霸王，抛弃他们更为温和的同龄人所表现出的顺从和谦恭。

你是个反对派吗？这也可以成为一种优势，当每个人都告诉你你无法成功时，你的反对派本性结合一点常识就能让你证明他们是错的。那担心呢？作为一个爱担心的人，我会第一个承认，担心确实有一些不健康的方面。但焦虑可以让你通过心理上回顾不同的情境来预测可能性，即使这些情境是负面的。而这并不完全是坏事。稍微担心一下，然后重新构建你的思维以平静你的大脑，就像我们之前讨论的那样，这是个不错的选择。至于天真的梦想家呢？如果你天真，和更务实的人合作是个不错的主意。但一点天真的梦想有助于让世界朝着积极的方向前进。没有人会想放弃这一点。

Based on all of this, what seemingly bad characteristic do you have that might have a good side to them? Join the discussion forum and let other people know and see what intriguing traits other people have.
根据以上内容，你认为自己有哪些看似不好的特质可能也有积极的一面？欢迎加入讨论论坛，与其他人分享，并看看其他人有哪些有趣的特质。



### 3-10 The Intelligence of Emotions

For a long time, emotions were considered unreliable compared with cognition. This has all changed in the last few decades. Emotions are important for social interactions, learning, and decision making. Emotions are complex brain states, associated with positive and negative experiences, and they are accompanied by facial expressions. Darwin wrote a book about visual expression as a form of communication that is important for survival, and natural selection. Paul Ekman is the world's leading expert on facial expression.
长期以来，情绪被认为相较于认知不可靠。但在过去几十年里，这种看法发生了改变。情绪在社交互动、学习和决策中都起着重要作用。情绪是复杂的脑状态，伴随着积极和消极的体验，并伴有面部表情。达尔文曾写过一本关于面部表情作为一种生存和自然选择重要沟通方式的书。保罗·艾克曼是全球面部表情方面的顶尖专家。

He was the real world inspiration for Cal Lightman in the TV drama series Lie to me,although Paul is lot nicer person than Cal.
他是电视剧《谎言之地》中卡尔·莱特曼的现实世界灵感来源，尽管保罗比卡尔要好得多。

Ekman went to Papua New Guinea to find out if pre-industrial cultures responded emotionally with the same facial expressions that we do. He found six universal expressions of emotion in all human societies that he studied. Happiness, sadness, anger, surprise, fear, and disgust.
艾克曼前往巴布亚新几内亚，想了解前工业文化是否用与我们相同的面部表情来响应情绪。他发现了六种在他研究的所有人类社会中普遍存在的情绪表达：快乐、悲伤、愤怒、惊讶、恐惧和厌恶。

Emotions are typically slow in onset and can last for a long time. Can you remember the last time that you got angry? How long did the angry mood last?
情绪通常发展缓慢，并且可能持续很长时间。你能记得上一次生气是什么时候吗？那种愤怒的情绪持续了多久？

There are groups of neurons very deep in the brain stem called neuromodulatory systems that control your levels of arousal, motivation, and attention.
大脑干深处有一群神经元，称为神经调节系统，控制着你的唤醒水平、动机和注意力。

Last week, we saw that one of them, the serotonin system, was important for regulating social interactions. Another brain stem system that fans out over wide regions of the brain, uses a chemical called noradrenaline.
上周，我们看到其中一个神经调节系统，即血清素系统，对调节社交互动很重要。另一个在大脑广泛区域扩散的脑干系统使用一种叫去甲肾上腺素的化学物质。

Edronax is a drug that works along the lines of Prozac, except that it is a reuptake inhibitor for noradrenaline, and it increases its activity.
Edronax是一种与普乐可复（Prozac）类似的药物，不同之处在于它是去甲肾上腺素的再摄取抑制剂，并增加其活性。

It could be more effective than Prozac in helping patients who are depressed and lack the capacity for sustained motivation. Whereas, serotonin activation results in serenity and mellowness, noradrenaline activity is involved in increasing drive motivation. When a closely related molecule manufactured in your adrenal gland, called adrenaline, is released in your blood, it makes your heart pound faster and prepares your body for vigorous physical activity, paralleling the increase in mental activity triggered by noradrenaline inside the brain.
它可能比普乐可复（Prozac）更有效，帮助那些感到抑郁并缺乏持续动机的患者。而血清素的活化会导致宁静和温和，去甲肾上腺素的活动则涉及到驱动动机的增加。当一种在你的肾上腺中制造的密切相关的分子——肾上腺素释放到血液中时，它会使你的心跳加速，为剧烈的身体活动做好准备，这与去甲肾上腺素在大脑内触发的精神活动增加相平行。

Is depression caused by imbalances in serotonin or in noradrenaline? These ancient neural systems interact with one another like players in an orchestra. So part of a serotonergic drug's efficacy, may be indirect by altering levels of noradrenaline. This interaction complicates the search for effective treatments for mental disorders, and reminds us, that although we talk about this or that chemical system, brain systems are deeply integrated. There is another powerful motivational system in the brain that uses dopamine, and is centered in the few groups of cells in the midbrain. This system of dopamine neurons underlies both the motivational and the emotional facets of extraversion.
抑郁症是由血清素或去甲肾上腺素的不平衡引起的吗？这些古老的神经系统相互作用，就像乐队中的乐器一样。因此，血清素类药物的部分疗效可能是通过间接改变去甲肾上腺素水平来实现的。这种相互作用使得寻找有效的心理疾病治疗方法变得复杂，同时也提醒我们，尽管我们谈论这个或那个化学系统，但大脑系统是深度整合的。还有另一个强大的动机系统，它使用多巴胺，集中在中脑的少数神经元群体中。这个多巴胺神经元系统支撑了外向性的人格特质的动机和情感方面。

High dopamine levels puts people in a good mood, energizes some people to seek out new worlds, and to go boldly where no one has gone before. But not too high a level since that leads to Tourette Syndrome, characterized by uncontrolled ballistic movements, and a blue streak of swear words, which you can imagine on your own. Your dopamine neurons can be interrogated when you need to make a decision. What should I order from the menu? You imagine each item, and your dopamine cells provide an estimate of the expected reward.
高多巴胺水平使人心情愉快，激励一些人去探索新领域，勇敢地迈向前所未有的地方。但不能过高，因为这会导致妥瑞氏症，其特征是无法控制的突然动作和不断冒出的脏话，这一点你可以想象。在你需要做决定时，你的多巴胺神经元会被激活。例如，当你想从菜单上点菜时，你会想象每个菜品，而你的多巴胺细胞则会提供对预期奖励的评估。

Should I marry this person? Your dopamine cells will give you a gut opinion that is more trustworthy than reasoning.
“我该嫁给这个人吗？”你的多巴胺细胞会给你一个直觉上的看法，这比推理更值得信赖。

Problems with many incommensurate dimensions are the most difficult to decide. For example, how do you trade off a sense of humor, a good dimension, with being messy, a bad dimension? Or hundreds of other comparisons. Your reward system reduces all these dimensions down to a common currency, the transient dopamine signal. Dopamine is a central part of reinforcement learning, which occurs when you associate a sensory input with a reward. Such as Pavlov's dog, in which food odors are are associated with salivation. Dopamine is released in the brain when an unexpected reward occurs, and dopamine levels are reduced from baseline, when an expected reward is not received. Dopamine neurons receive inputs from a part of the brain called the basal ganglia, which evaluates cortical states and assigns value to them, and is involved with learning sequences of motor actions to achieve a goal. Although this form of learning might seem simple, it has now been shown that reinforcement learning is the basis for the most powerful artificial intelligence system ever created. It is not just your cognitive systems, but also the impetus provided by your emotional systems that make you intelligent. Go is an ancient game that is highly popular in Asia. The 19 by 19 Go board is much larger than the 8 by 8 chessboard, which makes it possible to have several battles raging in different parts of the board, white against black pieces, vying for territory.
许多具有不可比性维度的问题是最难决定的。例如，你如何在幽默感（一个优点）和邋遢（一个缺点）之间进行权衡？或者数百种其他比较。你的奖励系统将所有这些维度归纳为一个共同的货币，即瞬时的多巴胺信号。多巴胺是强化学习的核心部分，当你将感官输入与奖励联系在一起时，这种学习就会发生。例如，巴甫洛夫的狗中，食物气味与唾液分泌相关联。当意外奖励发生时，大脑中会释放多巴胺，而当预期的奖励未能获得时，多巴胺水平会从基线下降。多巴胺神经元接收来自大脑一个叫做基底神经节的部分的输入，该部分评估皮层状态并为其分配价值，并参与学习一系列的运动行为以实现目标。虽然这种学习形式看似简单，但现在已显示出，强化学习是迄今为止最强大的人工智能系统的基础。不仅是你的认知系统，还有由你的情感系统提供的动力，使你变得聪明。围棋是一种古老的游戏，在亚洲非常流行。19乘19的围棋棋盘比8乘8的国际象棋棋盘大得多，这使得在棋盘的不同部分可以进行多场战斗，白棋与黑棋争夺领土。

Go is to chess in difficulty, as chess is to checkers. If chess is a battle, Go is a war. It has been thought that Go was so difficult that no computer program could ever play at championship level. However, this changed when the Korean Go world champion played a match with AlphaGo, a program based on reinforcement learning that played itself many millions of times. It came as a shock to many when AlphaGo won the first three games, winning the match, and exhibiting an an unexpectedly high level of play. The three neuromodulatory systems based on serotonin, noradrenaline, and dopamine interact strongly with the emotional systems in the brain. Without them, we would not be human. With them, we are able to form social bonds, evaluate dangerous situations, and learn new skills.

围棋的难度与国际象棋相比，就如同国际象棋与跳棋的关系。如果国际象棋是一场战斗，那么围棋就是一场战争。人们曾认为围棋如此困难，以至于没有任何计算机程序能够达到冠军级别。然而，当韩国围棋世界冠军与AlphaGo进行比赛时，这一观点发生了改变。AlphaGo是一款基于强化学习的程序，它进行了数百万次自我对弈。AlphaGo在首场三局比赛中获胜，并最终赢得比赛，展现出意想不到的高水平表现，这让许多人感到震惊。基于血清素、去甲肾上腺素和多巴胺的三种神经调节系统与大脑中的情感系统有着强烈的相互作用。没有它们，我们就无法成为人类。有了它们，我们能够形成社会纽带、评估危险情况并学习新技能。

I often wondered why Spock, on Star Trek, had such a flat affect. Could it be his neuromodulators were low? Think about it.
我常常想，斯波克在《星际迷航》中为何表现得如此冷淡。他的神经调节剂会不会太低？想一想吧。



### 3-11 Week 3 Wrap Up

This week we've talked about how careers get launched and how your own career can develop and change through your life. Your own internal feelings about what you want to do, of course, can play a critical role in your long term happiness. But society and culture can also have a dramatic affect on your career choices and decisions. As can your parents, family, and friends.
本周我们讨论了职业是如何起步的，以及你自己的职业如何在一生中发展和变化。当然，你对自己想做的事情的内心感受在你长期的幸福中起着至关重要的作用。但社会和文化也会对你的职业选择和决定产生显著影响，父母、家庭和朋友也是如此。

Given all this, and also given the nature of the real world, it's often valuable to carefully assess whether the learning you're doing with relation to your career might be putting you into a passion trap. That is whether you may be pursuing an interest you like, that teachers, professors, friends tell you is great, but which in reality may put you in debt while providing little opportunity for growth or comfort in the long term. Second skilling yourself using a pi rather than a T shaped way of cultivating knowledge related to your career, is a great approach. Sometimes, simply being okay at several or even a lot of things can be better than being a superstar at only one thing. For example, you can be one of the most brilliant coders in the world, but if you don't know how to read people enough to negotiate a good salary, you can't really benefit appropriately from your great skill.
鉴于这一切，以及现实世界的性质，仔细评估与职业相关的学习是否可能让你陷入热情陷阱常常是有价值的。也就是说，你可能正在追求一个你喜欢的兴趣，这个兴趣被老师、教授、朋友告诉你是很棒的，但实际上可能会让你背负债务，同时在长期内提供的增长或舒适的机会很少。以π形而不是T形的方式来提升与职业相关的知识是一种很好的方法。有时，仅仅在多个甚至很多方面做到还不错，可能比在某一领域成为超级明星更好。例如，你可能是世界上最优秀的程序员之一，但如果你不知道如何有效地与人沟通以谈判出一个好的薪水，你就无法真正从你的卓越技能中受益。

Sometimes people you know can be opposed to new learning that you may wish to do, or changes regarding your career. There are three ways to handle this opposition. Dabbling, leading a double life or being a contrarian. All three approaches have their advantages and disadvantages. We learned that sometimes selective ignorance can be better than general competence. After all, you don't want to be caught up fulfilling other peoples' desires while neglecting your own. In fact, sometimes your worst traits can be your best traits. Being disagreeable, a contrarian, a worrier or a dreamer can have positive sides that can be beneficial in the long run. If you use these traits wisely, feeling like an impostor isn't necessarily a bad thing at all. It leaves you more open and flexible, and helps you to avoid the over confidence that can sometimes lead to disaster. We also stepped back to look at the neuroscience of how we interact with others. The three neuromodulatory systems, based on serotonin, noradrenaline, and dopamine, help form the emotional systems of the brain. These systems, in turn, help us to form social bonds, evaluate dangerous situations, and learn new skills.
有时，你认识的人可能会反对你想要进行的新学习或职业上的变化。处理这种反对意见有三种方法：浅尝辄止、过着双重生活或采取反对的态度。这三种方法各有其优缺点。我们了解到，有时选择性无知可能比一般能力更好。毕竟，你不希望被卷入满足他人期望的漩涡中，而忽视了自己的需求。实际上，有时你最糟糕的性格特征也可以是你最好的特征。持不同政见、反对的态度、忧虑或做梦者，这些特质在长期内可能会有积极的一面。如果你明智地利用这些特质，感到像个冒名顶替者并不一定是坏事。这让你更加开放和灵活，并帮助你避免有时会导致灾难的过度自信。我们还退后一步，观察了我们与他人互动的神经科学。基于血清素、去甲肾上腺素和多巴胺的三种神经调节系统有助于形成大脑的情感系统。这些系统反过来帮助我们建立社会联系、评估危险情况和学习新技能。

One more thing. Don't forget the golden rule of career catastrophes. It's never as bad as you think it is at the time and there's always a silver lining. See you next week for the exciting course wrap up.
还有一件事。不要忘记职业灾难的黄金法则：在当时情况并不如你想象的那么糟糕，总会有一线希望。下周见，期待激动人心的课程总结。

Or if you're using something, like you're trying to remember a year, or a PIN code, or a birthday, very short numbers that have to be attached to someone, or some fact, or some thing. That's a different process as well and that's probably easier. Let's start with a few examples of how to remember small numbers to singular facts. Let's go. But one links to the other back and forward and that one was really easy. Well I want you to picture is someone really high up hanging now they are hanging by their nose. And then finally we had a will that you're on a tower, you lose it. Now, so check this out, the five things that you memorize were some of the tallest buildings in the world and their heights.
大家好！欢迎来到另一个记忆技巧视频。我是Nelson Dells，四届美国记忆冠军。在这个视频中，我将教你如何记住数字。

数字的特点就是难记。很多人出于某种原因很难记住数字。这是因为数字是非常抽象的，对吧？它们是代表数字的符号，但除此之外，它们只是符号。单独来看，这些符号、这些数字是没有意义的。因此，记住数字的首要目标是赋予数字意义。那么，Nelson，我们该怎么做呢？我将向你展示。

我们记住数字的第一件事是需要一个系统。我们需要某种方法将那些困难的、抽象的符号、数字转换成我们可以处理的东西，然后转化为我们可以想象或视觉化的东西。而最容易视觉化的就是单词，因此我们需要一个将数字转换为单词的系统。为了构建单词，我们需要字母。所以我有一个完美的系统，您很快就能记住数字，我需要一些工具，让我们开始吧。

这被称为主要系统。这个系统将每个数字（0到9）转换为辅音音素。0是s或z音，1是t或d音，2是n，3是m，4是r，5是l，6是j、ch或软g音，7是k、ch或硬g音，8是f或v，9是p或b。首先，你需要记住这一点。

让我们从0开始，z音，对吧？1的t或d音，画一个下划线。画一个t或d就是往下画。2的n，3的m，4的r，5的l，5根手指给你一个l。如果我这样画j，看看，这有点像倒过来的6。7，如果我画一个大写的K，看看，那就是两个7，背对背。如果我画一个草写的f，它看起来像一个8。最后，9，把它翻转，我得到了p，如果我翻转它，我得到了b。

好的，让我们试一个数字，比如54。5是l，对吧？4是r。所以我们有l和r，现在这打开了许多可能性，我们可以在前面、之间或后面加上元音，随便组合出许多单词，比如lure、lawyer、l(aye)r、l(ai)r、l(au)r(a)。记住，这些都是按声音来判断的。因此，即使像l(awye)r这样的单词在l和r之间有awye，你也要想，好吧，这并不是严格意义上的元音，尽管它是一个元音音。重要的是声音，对吧？所以l(awye)r。你听到的主要辅音音是l和r。因此，当你听到lawyer，或者看到lawyer时，你会将这两个辅音音解码为代表5和4的字母。

现在，这个数字不会在你的记忆中留下深刻印象，除非你将它与某些东西联系起来。根据你试图记住的内容，如果是数字序列，我们可能需要使用你的身体方法，或者像我在其他视频中提到的那样使用记忆宫殿。如果你试图记住的是年份、密码或生日这样的非常短的数字，那么将其附加到某个人、某个事实或某个事物上是一个不同的过程，这可能更简单。

让我们开始一些示例，看看如何记住小数字和单个事实。首先，我想让你想象一个汉堡包，这个汉堡包有手臂，它正在敲一个小钟，就像你敲前门一样，发出“tick”的声音。这汉堡包在敲一个小钟。所以当我说“汉堡”时，你想到的是“敲”、“tick”。如果我说“敲”、“tick”，你可以告诉我这是一个汉堡。这样一来，这个形象就会相互联系。这个联想非常简单。

接下来，我想让你想象一个人高高地挂着，挂着的是他的鼻子。他是用鼻子悬挂的，这个游戏很重要。好吧，接下来，我想让你想象一个简单的图像，交易，一个狗笼。你有一个大的铁丝狗笼，里面可能有一只脏狗。你正在和某人来回交易这个狗笼，你把它给他们，他们又把它还给你。

下一个图像，我想让你想象的是抚摸一扇有烟雾从缝隙中散发出来的门。你可能在抚摸这扇门，而在另一边，可能有火焰或者煤气泄漏，烟雾从门缝中散发出来。抚摸、门、烟雾。

最后，我想让你想象一个遗嘱。你有这个遗嘱，上面写着你所有的最后愿望，而你在一座塔的顶部，把它掉了。遗嘱、塔、丢失。

快速回顾一下：我们有汉堡在敲小钟；挂着鼻子，是个游戏；交易狗笼；抚摸有烟雾的门；最后你在塔上，丢失了遗嘱。现在，看看你记住的这五件事情，它们是世界上最高建筑及其高度。

Now here's how it goes, the first word was a word to help you remember the name of the building. Those are the two words, represented a four-digit number, which represents the height in feet. 现在，让我们来看看如何记住这些建筑的高度。第一个词是一个帮助你记住建筑名称的单词。这两个词代表一个四位数，表示高度（以英尺为单位）。第一个是汉堡，所以是哈利法塔（Burj Khalifa）。它的高度是“敲、滴”。如果我们将其分解成辅音音，"敲"代表n和k音，即2和7。"滴"代表1和另一个7，因此2717。哈利法塔的高度是2717英尺，哇，确实是世界上最高的建筑。

列表中的下一个是上海塔（Shanghai Tower），位于中国上海。你是用鼻子挂着的，而且是个游戏。从鼻子的n和s得到的数字是2和0，而“游戏”的g是7，所以是一个硬g，3则是游戏的结束，所以是2073英尺高的上海塔。

接下来是交易，你猜到了吗？纽约市的一号世界贸易中心（One World Trade Center）。这实际上很容易记住，即使不使用系统。它的高度是1776，这是美国历史上一个非常值得纪念的年份。但如果你想使用这个系统，请保持一致。我们有在交易的狗笼。狗笼的D是1，硬g又是7。笼子里的猫是7，软g是6，所以1776英尺高。

下一个是你在抚摸的东西，那是吉隆坡的双子塔（Petronas Towers），它是世界上最高的建筑之一。我们在抚摸什么呢？一扇有烟雾散发的门，对吧？所以D是1，R是4，所以是14。而“烟雾”是8和3，因此是1483。双子塔的高度是1483英尺。

最后是威利斯塔（Willis Tower），以前称为西尔斯塔（Sears Tower），其高度记得吗？我们在塔上并且丢失了。塔是T和R，这代表1和4，而“丢失”是5和0。因此威利斯塔的高度是1450英尺。

如果你想做任何事情，比如某个日期发生过的事情，你可以记住那个年份的高度，或者将你的PIN码与银行或任何其他机构的图像关联起来，或者将生日与某个人关联，想象力没有限制，我的朋友。

### Optional Bonus Video: Nelson Dellis Memory Tips #4 Remembering Names & Faces

What's up everyone? Welcome to another episode of Random Memory Tips. And in this episode, we're going to talk about how to remember names and faces.  So, how many of you out there think you have an especially poor memory for names and faces?  Probably a lot of you, that's probably the number one request I get is, Nelson how do I remember the names and faces of people I meet. Everybody seems to struggle with names and faces, but why? Why is it that names are so, here's the thing problem with remembering people's names and faces. One is that we're always on the move, right? When we meet people, it's either really quick, it's maybe really loud. The social situation actually dictates how easy or difficult it is to remember someone's name. And because there's people involved, we're often too embarrassed to ask for the name multiple times, or to follow up and really learn the person's name if we missed it or just forgot it really quick. But here's a cool thing, when I started memory techniques I had a bad memory. And especially a bad memory in names and faces, that was one of my worst skills. It turns out that after a number of years of practice I managed to become the top memorizer of names in the entire country. And when I do speeches I frequently will remember the whole room and go around picking people off, telling them what their name was. And I only have to meet them for a matter of seconds beforehand. I tell you that, so that you can realize that someone who didn't have a good memory, especially with names, can turn into someone who is really good at remembering names. Anyways I have five steps that I always follow, when memorizing names, I'm going to share them with you.  All right, step 1, pay attention. I already alluded to this beforehand, but you always have to pay attention. Remembering anything, especially names, will not happen unless your mind is ready to remember this person's name. An easy little tip here to get your mind primed to remember someone's face, is walk into the situation. Whether it's a meeting or you're walking into a party, or someone's about to introduce you. In your mind tell yourself the following phrase. I want to remember this person's name. That's it, if you just did that step alone and didn't even bother with the next four that I'm going to share, you would have a better memory for names, pay attention. All right, step 2 is to choose a feature. Most people might say, choose a feature on the person's face. Try to choose something that doesn't change, like don't use glasses, don't use earrings. I think choose whatever you notice first. If it is a pair of glasses, if it's a mole, if it's their bushy eyebrows, if it's their crazy red curly hair. Even if it's a funny shirt with a seagull on it with a hat, just choose it. It can even be more vague than that, it could be like the way that they walk, manner in which they move their hands. What's important to this is to choose something that you just naturally notice, and that popped out at you first. Why? Because that's probably what's going to pop out at you the next time you see them. All right, step 3, take their name and turn it into a picture. You've mentality primed yourself, you've chosen a feature and now you're going in for the handshake. Now you take that word, and you have to turn that into a picture. So, the first thing you want to do is say to yourself when you hear that name, what does it remind me of? If I heard Bob, for me I would think of a sea bob, so this round bob thing in the water bouncing up and down. Step 4, now this is the crucial step. This is what will cement that name into your memory, and that is where you intertwine steps two and three. Where you take the feature, you take the image, and you just match them together.  Imagine the picture interacting, or living, or being on that feature. So, the final step now is step number 5. And this is where you can consolidate all of that information and try to push it into your long-term memory. Step 5 is to review, and by review, I mean make an extra effort to think about or test yourself on this person's name. The key to having something engrained into your long-term memory is review, unfortunately. That is always going to be the case. The techniques one through four will get you very, very far, but if you want to have an incredible memory where you meet someone a year later. And you remember their names, and you just wow them, that's where a better review comes in. To review, we have those five steps. The first one was, to pay attention. The second one was, choose a feature. The third one was, ask for the name and come up with a picture for that name. Four is to mash the name and the feature together, and then five is review. I want to do some examples, I'm going to have you memorize the names and faces of five different English bulldogs. Why English bulldogs? Well, because they have such friendly faces. You could do this for a bar of soap. But of course you're going to want to use it for real live people. Okay, so I'm going to picture that even though she has a snaggle tooth, it's kind of menacing showing that tooth, she's the nicest dog that I've ever met. So with the snaggle tooth, you'd think she bite, maybe, with that sharp tooth. But in fact, she's actually really nice. 大家好！欢迎来到另一个随机记忆技巧的节目。在这一集中，我们将讨论如何记住名字和面孔。那么，有多少人觉得自己在记名字和面孔方面特别差呢？可能很多人，这可能是我收到的第一请求：Nelson，我该如何记住我遇到的人的名字和面孔。每个人似乎都在为名字和面孔而苦恼，但为什么会这样呢？为什么名字这么难记呢？

记住人们名字和面孔的问题有几个。首先，我们总是在移动中，对吧？当我们遇到别人时，情况往往很快，可能也很嘈杂。社交环境实际上会影响我们记住某人名字的难易程度。而且由于涉及到其他人，我们常常因为害怕尴尬而不敢多次询问名字，或者在错过了名字后也不愿意追问并真正记住这个人的名字。

但这里有个很酷的事情：当我开始学习记忆技巧时，我的记忆力很差，特别是记名字和面孔，这是我最差的技能之一。经过多年的练习，我竟然成为了全国记忆名字的顶尖高手。当我演讲时，我常常能记住整个房间的人，并告诉他们的名字，而我只需在之前见他们几秒钟。我告诉你这一点，是让你明白一个曾经记忆力差的人，尤其是在记名字方面，也能变得非常擅长记住名字。

无论如何，我有五个步骤，每次记名字时我都会遵循这些步骤，现在分享给你们。

**步骤1：注意力集中。** 我之前提到过这一点，但你必须时刻保持注意力。记住任何东西，特别是名字，只有在你的脑子准备好记住这个人的名字时才能实现。这里有一个小窍门，可以帮助你准备好记住某人的面孔：进入社交场合，无论是会议、派对，还是有人要介绍你。心里告诉自己一句话：“我想记住这个人的名字。”就这样，如果你只做到这一点而不去管接下来的四个步骤，你的记忆力也会有所提升，专注于注意力。

**步骤2：选择一个特征。** 大多数人可能会说，选择一个人的面部特征。尽量选择那些不会改变的东西，比如不要用眼镜、耳环。我觉得选择你第一次注意到的东西。如果是一副眼镜、一个痣、浓密的眉毛，或者疯狂的红色卷发，甚至是一件印着海鸥的搞笑衬衫，只需选择它。你可以选择更模糊的东西，比如他们走路的方式，或者手的动作。重要的是选择你自然注意到的东西，最先引起你注意的特征。为什么呢？因为那可能是你下次见到他们时首先注意到的东西。

**步骤3：将他们的名字转化为图像。** 你已经准备好了心态，选择了特征，现在要去握手。现在你要将这个名字转化为图像。你要问自己，当你听到这个名字时，它让我想起什么？如果我听到“Bob”，我会想起“海藻”（sea bob），也就是水中上下漂浮的那个圆圆的东西。

**步骤4：这是关键步骤。** 这一步将把名字牢牢地刻在你的记忆中，那就是将步骤二和三结合起来。你要把特征和图像结合在一起。想象这个图像在那个特征上互动、生活或存在。

**步骤5：复习。** 这是将所有信息整合并尝试推入长期记忆的步骤。复习的意思是特别努力地想一想或者测试一下这个人的名字。将某些东西铭刻在长期记忆中的关键是复习，不幸的是，这始终是如此。步骤一到四将使你走得很远，但如果你想在一年后遇到某人时记住他们的名字，并令他们惊叹，那就需要更好的复习。

现在让我们回顾一下这五个步骤。第一步是注意力集中。第二步是选择特征。第三步是询问名字并为该名字想出一个图像。第四步是将名字和特征结合在一起，第五步是复习。

我想做一些例子，我将让你记住五只不同的英语斗牛犬的名字和面孔。为什么是英语斗牛犬？因为它们的面孔非常友好。我想证明的是，理想情况下，使用这五个步骤，你可以对植物、狗、任何其他动物进行记忆。你也可以对一块肥皂进行记忆。但当然，你希望将其用于真实的人。然而，如果你能对其他一些稍微疯狂的东西做到这一点，那么在记住一个人的名字时，你肯定会有出色的记忆。准备好了吗？

好的，我们的第一只斗牛犬将是这只。比如，我可能选择这只狗的左耳。所以，我选择这个位置，他的棕色耳朵。这只狗的名字是Brian，所以我们需要将名字Brian转化为图像。Brian让我想到大脑（brain），Brian和brain非常接近。所以我将在这只斗牛犬的棕色左耳上放一个刚从头骨里出来的脑子。就这样。

第二只狗是这只。这只狗看起来有点老，很多肉。对于这只狗，我要选择的特征是它的下颚非常下垂。它的名字是Edward。当我想到Edward时，我想到的是“奖”（award）。Edward，award，Edward，award，差不多吧？所以，也许这只狗得到了历史上最下垂的脸的奖项。

这是我们的下一只狗。首先，我注意到这只狗的左边有一颗小的尖牙。因此，这只狗是女孩，她的名字是Janice。我在这个词中看到的或听到的是“nice”。所以，我会想象，即使她有一颗尖牙，显得有点吓人，但她是我见过的最可爱的狗。所以，尽管有那颗尖牙，你可能会想她会咬人，但实际上她真的很友好。

我们的下一只狗，非常可爱，我注意到的第一件事是这只狗的舌头在外面垂着。这只狗的名字是Leah。当我想到Leah这个名字时，我想到的是公主莱雅（Princess Leia）。所以，当我想到公主莱雅时，我就会想到她耳边的两个发髻。于是我会把这两个发髻放在这只狗的头上。她在舔着这两个发髻，就像公主莱雅一样。

最后一只狗，我选择了它的鼻子。它有一条更明显、不寻常的皮肤褶皱。所以，我会选择这个特征。它的名字是Phillip。Phillip听起来像是我要填充某样东西。因此，我们可以想象填满那条褶皱的皮肤，或者可能是装满水。

好了，现在我们来做一个快速测试。我将按顺序显示这五只狗，给你几秒钟时间大声说出名字，然后我会揭示答案。准备好了吗？

So that's it guys, that's how to remember names. Just stick to those five tips, when you're in social situation, and I promise you, you will improve. The important thing with names and faces is to try. So often we don't try anymore because we have these devices that can do it for us. Or we simply are too busy with ourselves or other things that we don't even take the time to try and learn a person's name. So take that time, make the effort, use that little thing that's inside your head and try to memorize people you meet. That's it for now, I'll see you in the next video. Thanks for watching, I'm out.
所以就是这样，伙计们，这就是记住名字的方法。在社交场合中坚持这五个技巧，我保证你会有所改善。记住名字和面孔的重要性在于要努力。我们常常不再尝试，因为我们有这些设备可以为我们做这些事情。或者我们只是太忙于自己的事情或其他事务，以至于连花时间去学习一个人的名字都没有。

所以花点时间，付出努力，利用你脑子里的那个小东西，尝试记住你遇到的人。这就是今天的内容，我们下个视频再见。感谢观看，我先走了。
